<answer>



Geez. Roy there is at least one exact answer to your question, and that is sleep apnea. While you are sleeping and going through your bio rythmns, your heart slows way down and momentarily stops several times during the night. When you get older and your system starts to age, it can forget or "misfire" during these periods and fail to restart the heart. This is sleep apnea. And the person dies. It is not a heart attack, although I suppose that this could occur. It is called sleep apnea and people die from it all the time.



</answer>

<question>



How many triple c's should I take?



I am going to take some triple c's before school today for my first time. I'm 6''2 and weigh 160. I have a pack of 8. Some people have told me to take all 8, some people told me to take just like 5 or 6. How many, from expirience, should I take?



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Before deciding to use this or ANY drug recreationally, whether your own script or over the counter, make sure you research it!!! I can't emphasize responsible use and harm reduction enough here. Telling someone not to do it is pretty pointless if they already have their mind made up, so its best to educate.



Anyways, Triple C's are Psuedoephedrine, and falling into the Ephedrine family, they have stimulant properties that are similar to but weaker then amphetamines.



The normal dosage is 60mgs or 2 tripple Cs. A safe recreational dosing would be 120 mgs or 4 tripples Cs (since this much comes in a slow release formula). Using high doses can cause hallucinations, sleeplessness, irritability, irregular heartbeat, dehydration, and physcosis, so be careful.  In extremely high doses, death has resulted.



Source(s):



Wiki, ewroids vault, my own experiences and medical studies, ect.



</answer>

<question>



Father A+, Mother A+, Brother A+ can the other sibling be B+?



What are the possible blood groups the son can have?



</question>



<answer from>



Rog P
Member since: 03 November 2008
Total points: 192 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



for sure even a F-



</answer>



<answer from>



Hamzay
Member since: 14 October 2006
Total points: 363 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Inheritance of blood type can be complicated. You may have group "A" blood, but have genes for both groups "A" and "O." Because "A" group is stronger or dominant, your blood will be group "A." However, you can give your children genetic material for either group "A" or "O." The same is true of "B" group. If both "A" and "B" genetic material is given to your child, the child will have group "AB" blood. A child with genes for "O" from both parents will be group "O." The chart on the following page shows this pattern.



Father's blood group  &



Mother's blood group  =  Child's blood group



O  & A



= O OR A
O  & B



= O OR B
O & AB  = A OR B
B & A



= O OR A OR AB



AB & A  = A OR B OR AB
B & B



= O OR AB
A & A



= O OR B



O & O  = O



So it depends on your father and mother entirely - the above wuz actually in a nice table form in the website which i refered to but couldnt paste the table here so i had to write it out for u



if u want u can visit the website source to view the table for your reference more clearly.



Source(s):



http://www.bloodonweb.com/bgroup.asp



</answer>

<answer from>



MS
Member since: 12 July 2008
Total points: 3149 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



Did you pull a muscle?  Try a hot bath.



It might be costochondritis.  Look that up, there's not much you can do for it.  I've provided you with a basic link to get you started....



Excerpt:



Costochondritis is an inflammation of the cartilage that connects a rib to the breastbone (sternum). It causes sharp pain in the costosternal joint — where your ribs and breastbone are joined by rubbery cartilage. Pain caused by costochondritis may mimic that of a heart attack or other heart conditions.



Your doctor might refer to costochondritis by other names, including chest wall pain, costosternal syndrome and costosternal chondrodynia. When the pain of costochondritis is accompanied by swelling, it's referred to as Tietze syndrome.



Most cases of costochondritis have no apparent cause. In these cases, treatment focuses on easing your pain while you wait for costochondritis to resolve on its own.



Source(s):



http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/costoch...



</answer>



<answer from>



The GIRL
Member since: 25 July 2008
Total points: 952 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



If you stop breathing, does the pain stop?



I sometimes get that, but only at a CERTAIN point in inhaling (about 3/4 of an inhale).
What i do is, breathe short/shallow, so it doesn't get to that painful point in the breath. it passes quickly.



If it's that, don't worry. It'll pass, and it's just your intercostal muscles (muscles between your ribs) freaking out. :) , which is nothing.



</answer>

<answer from>



donna d
Member since: 03 December 2007
Total points: 24580 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



i was put on it years ago but it brought down my white blood count so they took me right off it.but it is supposed to be an excellent drug for bipolar or depression.i know many people who take the drug and say it has helped them allot.



</answer>



<answer from>



Oscar C
Member since: 29 September 2008
Total points: 1492 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Depakote is a drug for the treatment of  manic episodes of bipolar disorder and for epilepsy, chronic pain associated with neuropathy and migraine headaches. Below are excerpts from Wikipedia:



"Valproate semisodium (INN) or divalproex sodium (USAN) consists of a compound of sodium valproate and valproic acid in a 1:1 molar relationship in an enteric coated form. It is used in the UK and U.S. for the treatment of the manic episodes of bipolar disorder, and increasingly taken long-term for prevention of both manic and depressive phases of bipolar disorder, especially the rapid-cycling variant. It is also used in the US for the treatment of epilepsy, chronic pain associated with neuropathy, and migraine headaches. Its chemical name is sodium hydrogen bis(2-propylpentanoate). The extended release formulation allows for a single daily dose.



In the UK semisodium valproate has been sold for a few years as the proprietary drug Depakote and marketed for psychiatric conditions only. It is about five times the price of sodium valproate, which has been marketed for around 30 years as Epilim by the same company for epilepsy and is also available from other manufacturers as a generic product."



My friend who has diabetic neuropathy had taken it and said that he encountered a mild case of vomiting, loss of appetite and a dark urine. But he had to discontinue upon doctor's advice.



Good luck to you.



Source(s):



Yahoo! and Wikipedia.



</answer>

You hurt your thigh while exercising, maybe before you had properly warmed up, usually you don't feel that pain until the next day.

Maybe you had a cramp while sleeping, but it didn't wake you up.

<answer from>



SassyLas...
Member since: 06 August 2008
Total points: 718 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Stay away from caffeinated beverages (coffee, sodas, teas) or foods (like chocolate or energy bars) after 6PM.  Don't exercise less than 2 hours before you'd be going to sleep.  In the hour or so before you want to go to sleep, just relax in a room that's warm, calm and the not too brightly lit.  Some suggestions for relaxing are to read, listen to mellow music, watch tv or movies, or meditate.



You can also try to play mellow calming music, or use one of those nature sound machines very lightly in the background as you try to go to sleep.  Also, we all have biorhythms that regulate our sleeping patterns and everyone's is different.  I find that if I go to bed too early that I will lay wide awake in bed for a longtime, whereas if I wait until 11:30 (or whatever time works for you) I can fall asleep within 10-15 minutes.



When I have a really bad bout of insomnia that lasts for a few days, I'll try and exercise a lot during the day so that I'll be tired when it's bedtime.  Something to consider is whether your insomnia occurs for more than 2 nights at a time.  Could there be things on your mind that keep you up?



</answer>

Dr. A

<answer>



there is no such serious risks as the whole procedure is done under aseptic technique and its very brief and minor. nothing to worry much infact you doing the most humanitarian act i believe. your doctor prior to donation shall explain the minor complications like infection or bleeding and the way to prevent them. otherwise its totally safe and quite helpful act. <answer from>



kgarther...
Member since: 03 November 2008
Total points: 166 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



No, you are not risking your life. However, if you are matched and chosen as a donor, the process of removing your bone marrow is a little painful. The will stick a coring needle into (usually) your hip bone to remove the marrow. It hurts but it is worth it! You will probably take ibuprofen for 2-3 days afterwards.

We're on to Tuesday (yesterday). ALL my symptoms were gone, besides the fact that now I'm just barely dizzy (only when I make sudden movements) and my throat hurts to swallow. This is not the kind of pain as in a sore, scratchy throat. This feels more like a pain in the far back roof of my mouth where I begin to swallow. Someone told me they had all these same symptoms, and after a day of the painful throat, they got better.

flingebu...

<answer from>



SassyLas...
Member since: 06 August 2008
Total points: 718 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Could be the flu or strepthroat.  Possibility tonsilitis.  Have you been taking your temperature.  You need to do that a couple times of day.  The sweating is a good sign that you have a fever and it breaks but then comes back.  However, you can get chills and sweats but still have a normal temperature, this is why you need to take your temperature to make sure.  Regardless, a fever for a few days is not good.



Say, "Ahhhh," and have someone check your throat for white splotches in the back (Strep) or inflamed tonsils.  If your throat is just red then it's more likely that you have the flu with a sore throat.  However, sometimes a really bad cold can simulate flu-like symptoms.



Either way, you should see a doctor to determine if you might have a viral or bacterial infection, which is treated differently.
---------------------
STREP
Sore throat that comes on rapidly.
Difficulty swallowing.
Headaches.
Fever, sometimes greater than 102° F.
A raw, red appearance to the back of the throat.
White pus on tonsils.
Tender, high lymph nodes in neck.
Rash.
Absence of a cough, stuffy nose, or other upper-respiratory symptoms.



Source(s):



http://www.webmd.com/cold-and-flu/unders...



</answer>

<question>



Can yoga help relieve anxiety?



I have a lot of anxiety and was thinking of trying yoga.



</question>



<answer from>



A)*Ang...
Member since: 09 October 2007
Total points: 3758 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



How to Stop Worrying
Self-Help Strategies for Anxiety Relief



Worrying can be helpful when it spurs you to take action and solve a problem. But if you’re preoccupied with “what ifs” and worst-case scenarios, worry becomes a problem of its own. Unrelenting doubts and fears are paralyzing, not motivating or productive. They sap your emotional energy, send your anxiety levels soaring, and interfere with your day-to-day life–all this with no positive payoff! The good news is that chronic worrying is a mental habit you can learn how to break. You can train your brain to stay calm and collected and to look at life from a more positive perspective.
In This Article:
Why is it so hard to stop worrying?



Accept uncertainty



Create a worry period



Challenge negative thoughts



Learn how to relax



Take care of yourself



Related links



Print  Authors
Text Size
Why is it so hard to stop worrying?
Why You Keep Worrying
You have mixed feelings about your worries. On one hand, your worries are bothering you - you can't sleep, and you can't get these pessimistic thoughts out of your head. But there is a way that these worries make sense to you. For example, you think:



Maybe I'll find a solution.



I don't want to overlook anything.



If I keep thinking a little longer, maybe I'll figure it out.



I don't want to be surprised.



I want to be responsible.



You have a hard time giving up on your worries because, in a sense, your worries have been working for you.



Source: The Worry Cure: Seven Steps to Stop Worry from Stopping You, Robert L. Leahy, Ph.D.
Constant worrying takes a heavy toll. It keeps you up at night and makes you tense and edgy during the day. You hate feeling like a nervous wreck. So why is it so difficult to stop worrying?



For most chronic worriers, the anxious thoughts are fueled by the beliefs–both negative and positive–they hold about worrying.



On the negative side, you may believe that your constant worrying is harmful, that it’s going to drive you crazy or affect your physical health. Or you may worry that you’re going to lose all control over your worrying–that it will take over and never stop.



On the positive side, you may believe that your worrying helps you avoid bad things, prevents problems, prepares you for the worst, or leads to solutions.



Negative beliefs, or worrying about worrying, add to your anxiety and keep worry going. But positive beliefs about worrying can be even more damaging. It’s tough to break the worry habit if you believe that your worrying protects you. In order to stop worry and anxiety for good, you must give up your belief that worrying serves a positive purpose. Once you realize that worrying is the problem, not the solution, you can regain control of your worried mind.



Worry and anxiety self-help tip #1: Accept uncertainty
The inability to tolerate uncertainty plays a huge role in anxiety and worry. Chronic worriers can’t stand doubt or unpredictability. They need to know with 100 percent certainty what’s going to happen. Worrying is seen as a way to predict what the future has in store, a way to prevent unpleasant surprises and control the outcome. The problem is, it doesn’t work.



Thinking about all the things that could go wrong doesn’t make life any more predictable. You may feel safer when you’re worrying, but it’s just an illusion. Focusing on worst-case scenarios won’t keep bad things from happening. It will only keep you from enjoying the good things you have in the present. So if you want to stop worrying, start by tackling your need for certainty and immediate answers.



Challenging intolerance of uncertainty: The key to anxiety relief
Ask yourself the following questions and write down your responses. See if you can come to an understanding of the disadvantages and problems of being intolerant of uncertainty.



Is it possible to be certain about everything in life?



What are the advantages of requiring certainty, versus the disadvantages? Or, how is needing certainty in life helpful and unhelpful?



Do you tend to predict bad things will happen just because they are uncertain? Is this a reasonable thing to do? What is the likelihood of positive or neutral outcomes?



Is it possible to live with the small chance that something negative may happen, given its likelihood is very low?



Adapted from Accepting Uncertainty, Centre for Clinical Interventions



Worry and anxiety self-help tip #2: Create a worry period
It’s tough to be productive in your daily life when anxiety and worry are dominating your thoughts. Trying to stop worrying doesn’t work - at least not for long. You can distract yourself for a moment, but you can’t banish your anxious thoughts for good. Trying to do so often makes them stronger. But that doesn’t mean there’s nothing you can do to control your worry. You just need to try a different approach. Rather than trying to totally suppress an anxious thought, develop the habit of postponing worrying.



</answer>

<answer from>



jill_vic
Member since: 17 March 2006
Total points: 1300 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Sorry to hear that you are not sleeping well - sadly either being unable to get off to sleep and/or waking up early can be part of depression.  I have had times of depression in my life, also am on the menopause now, so know all about bad sleep!



Maybe you could go and have a word with the doctor who prescribed those tablets, telling him/her that you still cannot sleep on them.  It may be that you could take a different tablet or take it at a different time of day.  I know that antidepressants like Prozac or Seroxat can cause sleeplessness if taken later in the day....I was on Amitryptilline (?spelling) when I had a bad time of depression, and that really helped me sleep if I took it before bed.



(That is a different and older sort of antidepressant than Prozac etc.)



One tablet that is available over the counter and should be safe for most people, is an antihistamine called Phenergan in the UK - it is cheap and if you take 25mg or so an hour before bed, it can help knock you out!  Nytol is similar, but costs more.  Ask at your local pharmacy, but mention what other tablets you are taking, just to be on the safe side.



My family doctor said it was good to have a regular bedtime routine, trying not to do anything too demanding (ie not chat online or do Yahoo answers!) for a couple of hours before bed, not too much caffeine late in the day, listen to music/watch TV/read before bed.....praying works for me!



Source(s):



Experience



</answer>



<answer from>



Carol
Member since: 28 March 2008
Total points: 141 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



I remember an exercise I was recommended back when i used to have the sleep issues.  Hope this would help you..



This would take you hardly 15- 20 minutes.  Before going to sleep, lie down on leveled surface without a pillow.  With eyes closed, try to get all of the worrying thoughts out of your mind.  Stretch your toes (not to the point that it causes discomfort for you), keep it so for a count of 10 or so, then relax the toes for another 2 minutes.



Next, do it with your calf muscles, tightening it and then relaxing the same way as above with counts.



Then your thighs and abdomen.



With chest, inhale in as much as air as you can and pause for a second and then exhale very slowly.  Do it for 2-3 times.



Next, lift up your head slight to a comforable level and then the counts as before.  Then, slowly relax it back.



Once you finish, try to loosen all your body muscles with eyes closed.  By now, you would feel a bit tired and a strong need to relax.  Lie down and relax for at least 10 minutes.  Leave all your worries and troubles out of your mind, imagine  a beautiful scenary or a natural place you would love to be at.  When you feel comfortable, slowly open your eyes.  I felt personally good after doing so for 2 weeks.



Hope this was of some help to you...



PS:  Please note that every time you do with each muscle, try to concentrate on that particular part of your muscle and forget about the sarrounding noises.



</answer>

The determinant of whether or not a person is lazy is not when or how much they sleep, but what they accomplish when they're awake.



Sleeping less should allow you to accomplish more, but if you can't function without the sleep, then get more sleep.



Needing more than 9 or 10 hours, however, indicates a problem.

<answer from>



birdshel...
Member since: 25 January 2007
Total points: 655 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



There are many reasons for having to sleep longer than 8 hours per night.



Some of the reasons for sleeping longer are given by others.  It is true that we are all different and all need varying amounts of sleep.  Of course, many of us wish we could sleep much less and there are a some folks who can do so.



There are also people who may have sleep disordered breathing (SDB). Most often, this will be obstructive sleep apnea (OSA). The ineffective sleep causes one to continue to be tired.  This can be fixed by a sleep study to determine if one has SDB.  The sleep study will then tell what treatment will help, if any is required.  In a case such as this, one couldn't be called lazy for sleeping more than usual.  One's body is simply requiring longer sleep to make up for a lack of quality sleep.



Sleep deprivation is serious.  Those who are sleep deprived drive a vehicle equivalently to one who is drunk, so there is no doubt that the lack of quality sleep is a great problem in this world.  Those who are heavier tend to have more SDB, so as our country becomes more obese, the sleep disorders become more common.



I used to sleep 12-14 hours, and then had a sleep study.  Now, I have a continuous positive airway pressure machine and a mask that I wear at night.  I now sleep about 8-9 hours a night, and I like sleeping less than half of my life away.  It has made a difference, and I no longer snore.  That is a plus!



Source(s):



Personal experience



</answer>



<answer from>



udaya k
Member since: 13 June 2008
Total points: 5428 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Not always.



</answer>

<question>



Known side-effects for ecstacy?



i've been taking 2-3 ecstacy pills daily for the past 4 weeks
i've been feeling great, but getting depressed easily when not on it



</question>



<answer from>



katie s
Member since: 10 April 2007
Total points: 3480 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Wow, yeah time to stop taking them and let your brain rest.



MDMA produces intense feelings of pleasure, empathy, warmth, and happiness. It also increases sensitivity to music, makes people more emotionally open, and has a stimulating, speedy physical effect.



When ecstasy is swallowed, the full effect is usually felt within one hour. It starts with tingling and little rushes of exhilaration. Some people may experience nausea or dizziness while coming up but it quickly passes.



The effect builds quickly, coming on in waves within the first two hours, strengthening with each pass. A lightness of mood and relaxation gives way to waves of physical pleasure, euphoria, openness and empathy to others around you. The awareness of touch is strongly heightened. The muscles relax.



The peak arrives and then the effects last 4-6 hours, with a gradual tapering come-down in the last two.



Jaw clenching and "clamping" is a common side-effect of E and many people get relief by chewing on dummies or gum, smoking cigarettes or sucking lollies.



top



in the brain
E causes serotonin (5-hydroxytryptamine or 5-HT) and dopamine to flood the brain. Both are neurotransmitters which influence the flow of information throughout the brain. Changing the balance between the two changes your mood. E gives you a glow of well-being, happiness, empathy, euphoria, increases your sensitivity to rhythmic music, and makes you want to dance.



The latest studies show that Ecstasy use can impair the serotonin system and memory performance. Please see our guide - Can Ecstasy Impair Your Memory? - plus safe dancing tips on how to protect yourself.



top



comedown



On come-down, you may feel physically and emotionally drained. Without the artificial stimulation of E, the body and mind can suffer from exhaustion and anxiety.



It's very important to have somewhere warm and comfortable to go back to, preferably stocked with refreshments, and gentle 'chill' music. General health and regularity of use play a very large part in the harshness of the after-effects.



Ecstasy is rapidly broken down by the liver but about 60% enters the urine unchanged. The urine could be drunk to recycle it, in the same way that Siberian tribesmen drink each other's urine after eating magic mushrooms. This is known in most circles as 'desperate'.



top



days after



The first day or two after taking E, senses are a little blunted, but a general sense of contentment can result in 'Happy Mondays.' E temporarily depletes serotonin for several days, which can prompt mood swings or mild depression.



Wednesday is usually the bleakest day before moods stabilise again. Often, weekly users do not regain neurochemical balance before they dose again. Permanently fluctuating moods can be a symptom of over-use.



Some users take the food supplement 5-HTP, a chemical precursor of serotonin (available from most health food shops), during, and after an E experience. It can help rebalance moods, as can tryptophyan-heavy foods such as bananas, milk, apples, turkey, chicken, yoghurt and chocolate.



Source(s):



http://www.thegooddrugsguide.com/ecstasy...



</answer>

<question>



If measles is so simple and according to lots that bed rest works  why do people still die iis 1 child to many?



SCHOOLBOY, 13, DIES AS MEASLES
MAKES A COMEBACK



The Sunday Times (London) April 2 2006



Brian Deer



A 13-YEAR-OLD boy has become the first person in Britain for 14 years to die of measles in a sign that the disease, once a common killer, is resurfacing.



The boy’s death is the first since the scare over the combined measles, mumps and rubella (MMR) vaccine caused a drop in immunisation rates.



The first death from acute measles infection since 2006 has been reported. A 17 year old with underlying congenital immunodeficiency was admitted to hospital with respiratory distress and pneumonia on 20 April following contact with a case of measles. The patient deteriorated and was transferred to ITU a week later with respiratory failure, but subsequently died (five weeks later). Serum samples and nasopharyngeal aspirates taken at various times have confirmed that the patient had infection with a strain identical to the measles strain (MVs/Enfield.GBR/14.07 genotype D4) that has now been circulating in the UK for over a year.



Due to almost 10 years of sub-optimal MMR vaccination



There were 61 infant deaths from measles 1905-1908. ..... compare the death rate for measles with other areas of the UK because the birth rate had ...



</question>



<answer from>



Dr Frank
Member since: 03 February 2007
Total points: 98064 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Women's Health



Diet & Fitness



Other - Health & Beauty



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Many of the once almost eradicated childhood diseases had a mortality due to the rarer complications. Both the diseases and the risk of this were reducing even before immunisation came in due to general increases in fitness and a waning of disease potency.



However the statistics that predicted in advance that a reduction in immunisation would reduce 'herd immunity' levels proved correct. The diseases began to appear in epidemic once more. Lack of early exposure tends to mean that when they do strike, they can be both more severe and have a higher risk of complications.



Potentially fatal complications of measles include pneumonia, meningitis and encephalitis and a death rate of as many as 1 in 2,500 cases of infection!



Mumps complications include, orchitis or oophoritis ( inflammation of the testicles or ovaries,) which can produce sterility. Also meningitis and encephalitis and pericarditis, all of which can be fatal.



Complications of Rubella include fits, pneumonia and encephalitis as well as the well known risks to the foetus in pregnant women who become infected.



Overall this of course reinforces the fact that the risks of the diseases always overwhelmed and small risks that the vaccines might pose.



Source(s):



GP for more years than I care to remember



</answer>

All 3 viruses covered by MMR can have a devastating impact. Measles kills, mumps causes male infertility and rubella causes terrible birth defects. Anyone considering refusing the MMR on behalf of their child should consider this. But maybe the NHS could meet such parents half way and offer them individual vaccines rather than the 3-in-1.

<answer from>



greydoc6
Member since: 11 November 2006
Total points: 16927 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



I think you mean there were 61 infant deaths from measles between 2005 - 2008. The death rate a hundred years ago would have been much greater.



In the US, measles was a leading cause of childhood death until about 1950, and even until the development of the vaccine. My career in pediatrics began before the availability of the measles vaccine, and I can tell you from personal experience that practically all of the affected children I saw with measles were quite ill with high fevers and coughs. Secondary pneumonia was a common complication.



Most fatalities occur in children under age two, especially those whose parents are below the poverty line. Vitamin A deficiency may be a contributing factor in these children.



Source(s):



Retired doc.



</answer>

mtwaites

<answer>



First you should consider doing something like physiotherapy and see if that problem would be able to help and assist you with your problem first. If this problem doesn't get better from doing some physiotherapy, then you should consider talking with an orthopedic surgeon about your case.

<answer from>



Alice B
Member since: 20 October 2008
Total points: 835 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Negative emotions (like sadness, stress, anger, etc.) causes your Serotonin production to be low; when your Serotonin level is low, you are more prone to getting Anxiety, Panic Attacks, Depression, etc.



Medication like Antidepressants (SSRI - Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitor) helps to boost Serotonin level.
But there are natural ways to do it without medication. There's this strange herb called "St John's Wort" - it is said to be more effective than Prozac. No, it is not for mild depression only and ignore those sayings. In fact, it does help anxiety and panic-attacks as St John's Wort works like prozac. Other natural ways will be exercise, diet, more exposure to light, etc.



The problem is that, even if your Serotonin is balanced... you have that "learned behavior" in your mind. You need to break that initial cycle to destroy that learned behavior - Cognitive Behavior Therapy (CBT) does this. A technique that you can use without CBT will be Distraction... There are several other techniques to help cope them!
Ok, to use Distraction: Firstly, try to....



Extracted from Source.



Source(s):



http://PanicAttackResearch.blogspot.com



</answer>

<answer from>



amy b
Member since: 07 June 2006
Total points: 249 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Having an overactive thyroid generally means your metabolism is increased and this can be dangerous with certain medications.  Medicines are made to metabolize at a certain rate, when conditions exist that effect the rate, problems could arise.  Glad you are going to your doctor

nursing

<answer>



With hyperthyroidism, your body metabolises certain products very quickly, certain medicines are designed to be released into the blood over a period of time, quicker metabolism could lead to a localised overdose, with exceptionally quick metabolisms, even normal doses of painkillers can cause acute liver failure
Im assuming you're medicated for your hyperthyroidism?

<question from>

<question>



What does this blood work order say?



I'm getting blood work to test for anemia but I cannot make out what this says. Help?



http://i36.tinypic.com/24mfd5x.jpg



</question>



<additional details>



This is what I have so far
1) CBC



6) TSH
2) ??GPT??
3) ???Looks like CBC again...
4) ?Something Ferric CBC
5) Vit B12



</additional details>



<answer from>



Lab Girl
Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 117 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Don't you just love doctor's writing?
Looks like it says:



- CBC (complete blood count)



- LFT (liver function test) maybe, hard to tell



- looks like either CBC again, or IBC (iron binding capacity).  They wouldn't do two CBC's, possibly just that the doctor was writing fast and wrote it twice.



- Iron, Ferritin, IBC (iron binding capacity)



- Vitamin B12



- TSH (thyroid stimulating hormone)



Hope that helps you!



</answer>

i couldnt go back to sleep i woke up at 9 to take it, and im a little anxious i am taking it for anxiety. idk if its because im thinking about all the side effects i could get or what not. how did you feel on your first day of taking wellbutrin? did it help for your anxiety? any info will help thank you!



</question>



<answer from>



armywife
Member since: 22 October 2006
Total points: 1498 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



when i started wellbutrin-I took one pill to start (at a low dose) for i believe a week...things felt good, then I up the dose to two pills a day as my Dr had instructed--this was too much for me. I was having strange scary dreams, my heart was pounding, I felt very jittery. Since then I have decided it was best that I stick to only one pill a day, I take it in the morning so that it doesn't keep me awake at night (you should take it before 5pm--if you are only taking one pill a day) Everyone is different so you'll have to base whats best for you on your reaction to the meds. This is just how it effected me. I've been on them for maybe 3 years...and I haven't had any issues since. I think they are great pills and I think the lowest dose is just the right dose for me. So just keep an eye on symptoms you get, write things down in a notebook if you must--but do keep track of everything you feel (both physically and mentally) Make notes of weird feelings and mention them to your dr.



</answer>

thnx



</asker's comment>

<answer from>



Tizzie
Member since: 18 November 2007
Total points: 6385 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Do you have a little bit of something stuck between tooth and gum?  This can cause swelling.



</answer>



<answer from>



Oscar C
Member since: 29 September 2008
Total points: 1464 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



In situations like this, it is always best to consult a dentist. There are many reasons for swollen gums, but the main cause would be infection. Your gums could have been infected (by bacteria, etc.) that's why it's swollen. While you say that it doesn't hurt and it is not bleeding, but if you don't do anything about it, then soon it will hurt and will be bleeding. As you said, you are a little run down and have a few mouth ulcers. For infection, you can always take a broad-spectrum antibiotics, but the best action would be to consult a dentist before the situation gets worse.



Good luck to you.



</answer>

<answer from>



Soie R
Member since: 30 September 2008
Total points: 1412 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Have you been tested for epilepsy?



There is a kind of seizure called an "absence seizure" which does the things you say has been happening to you ie black-outs, forgetting things etc.



With an absence seizure, you don't have any convulsions or any noticeable movements, but you can blank out for periods of 10 to 30 seconds and still appear to be conscious and aware of everything that is happening around you.



Being on the computer all the time, watching too much TV or playing too many Playstation, Nintendo, X-Box games etc can also cause seizures because of the constant flickering of the screen.



I would go to the doctor, explain your symptoms and asked to be checked thoroughly.



</answer>

<question>



Am I experiencing a common cold or the flu?



I had a sore throat yesterday. Today, I woke up and my throat was still sore until an hour later, it went away.



Now, instead of a sore throat, I have a stuffy nose!



Then, later on today, my head started to get hot and "sting" (probably fever).



Finally, I am aching all over, especially in the hips.



</question>



<additional details>



My nose is very sensitive, also. I will blow it, and it will become breathable but painful. Like my nose is so clear that the air stings it.

<answer from>



sunybuni
Member since: 28 July 2006
Total points: 4652 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Based on the possibility of a fever, I would guess flu.  Most people don't have a fever with a cold.  And the flu is an upper respiratory illness, so that would account for the stuffy nose.

1. Inhaling - take in air into your body through the nose
2. Retaining - hold your breath inside your body
3. Exhaling - blow out air from your body through the mouth



It is during deep sleep that growth hormone does its job of thickening and lengthening your bones. So appropriate sleeping time (not the longer, the better) and correct sleeping posture is very important for your body to grow. Sleep is defined as a natural periodic state of rest for the mind and body, in which the eyes usually close and consciousness is completely or partially lost, so that there is a decrease in bodily movement and responsiveness to external stimuli.



During deep sleep, growth hormone produced by your pituitary gland is released into your blood stream and travel through your body and causes the thickening and lengthening of your bones. Therefore, you should achieve "deep level" sleep on a daily basis in order to coordinate your affords of exercises and proper diet. The following are some helpful tips on how to easily achieve deep level sleep.



Sleep in a comfortable and firm mattress.
Sleep in a room that is dark, quiet and fresh smelling.
Sleep with clean, soft, and comfortable clothes.
Keep your hands and feet warm. Scientific studies have shown that warm hands and feet will help induce REM (rapid eye movement) deep sleep. Cold hands and feet will keep you from deep sleep.
Drink a big glass of water before going to bed and when you wake up; this will help clean out your system.
Practice total relaxation and deep breathing for a few minutes before you go to bed.
Relax from head to toe. Close your eyes and relax every part of your body.
Maintain a habit of sleeping at the same time everyday, including weekends.
Sleep on your back with a flat pillow under your knees. This will align your spine properly and prevent any back aches caused by sleeping in a bent position.

<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



It is possible that you are deficient in Zinc ....... deficiencies in Zinc can cause taste abnormalities ........ the most common deficiency symptoms include dry and rough skin, dull looking hair, brittle finger nails, white spots on nails, reduced taste and smell, loss of appetite, mood swings, reduced adaptation to darkness, frequent infections, delayed wound healing, dermatitis and acne.......... eat more foods rich in zinc ie ~ lean red meats, seafood (especially oysters), wheat germ, brewer's yeast, pumpkin seeds, eggs and ground mustard.



Phytates, compounds found in grains and legumes, bind with zinc so that it cannot be absorbed.



Things that will deplete your zinc supplies are alcohol, caffeine, antacids like mylanta, corticosteroids, diuretics and ulcer medications.

http://www.zinc.org/zinc_health.html

<answer from>



I wonder
Member since: 29 October 2008
Total points: 271 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Feeling down from time to time is a normal part of life. But when sadness takes hold and won't go away, it may be depression. More than just the temporary "blues," the lows of depression make it tough to function and enjoy life like you once did. A person with severe depression has little or no interest in work or hobbies, and may even have trouble getting out of bed.  With treatment and help, you can feel better. Learning how to understand depression – including its signs, symptoms, and causes – is the first step to overcoming the problem.



If you identify with several of the following signs and symptoms, and they just won’t go away, you may be suffering from clinical depression.



you can’t sleep enough or you sleep too much



you can’t concentrate or find that previously easy tasks are now difficult



you feel worthless and hopeless



you can’t control your negative thoughts, no matter how much you try



you have lost your appetite or you can’t stop eating



you are constantly irritated or become enraged even at small things – and this is new for you



you have thoughts that life is not worth living, or have a plan for how you would end it (Seek help immediately if this is the case)



Feelings of helplessness and hopelessness



A bleak outlook—nothing will ever get better and there’s nothing you can do to improve your situation.



Loss of interest in dailly activities



No interest in or ability to enjoy former hobbies, pastimes, social activities, or sex.



Appetite or weight changes



Significant weight loss or weight gain—a change of more than 5% of body weight in a month.



Sleep changes



Either insomnia, especially waking in the early hours of the morning, or oversleeping (also known as hypersomnia).



Psychomotor agitation or retardation



Either feeling “keyed up” and restless or sluggish and physically slowed down.



Loss of energy



Feeling fatigued and physically drained. Even small tasks are exhausting or take longer.



Self-loathing



Strong feelings of worthlessness or guilt. Harsh criticism of perceived faults and mistakes.



Concentration problems



Trouble focusing, making decisions, or remembering things.



The Many Faces of Depression
Depression comes in many shapes and forms.  In some, depression can persist at a low level for months and even years. In others, the symptoms are so strong that life grinds to a halt and suicide can be a real concern. Depression can be triggered or aggravated by personal and interpersonal events, hormonal changes (like after childbirth), and can even be triggered by lack of sunlight.



Clinical (Major) Depression



Major depression is characterized by the inability to enjoy life and experience pleasure. Lack of interest in outside activities, strong feelings of worthlessness or guilt, thoughts that life isn’t worth living, weight gain or loss, sleep troubles- all of these are signs of major depression. These feelings normally must persist for at least two weeks in order to be considered a major depressive episode. The symptoms can range from mild, when you can function in life with extra effort, to severe, where you can no longer complete daily activities.



Dysthymia (recurrent, mild depression)



If you have dysthymia, you may feel like you’ve always been depressed. In dysthymia, the depressive symptoms are not as strong as in a major depressive episode, but they last a long time, at least two years. More days than not, you feel mildly or moderately depressed, although you may have some temporary mood lifts. These chronic symptoms make it very difficult to enjoy life or to remember better times.



Postpartum Depression
Strong emotions after giving birth, “the baby blues”, are normal. New mothers are recovering from birth, are most likely sleep deprived, and are adjusting to the responsibilities of parenthood. Postpartum depression, however, is a longer lasting and more serious.  What can be especially terrifying to mothers suffering from postpartum depression are feelings of wanting to avoid or even harm the baby. Postpartum depression doesn’t have to occur right after delivery. It can occur up to a year after childbirth.



</answer>

<answer>



you had a panic attack .... i have them too sometimes



</answer>



<answer from>



Justin M
Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 113 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Many people who suffer panic attacks state they are the most frightening experiences of their lives. Sufferers of panic attacks report a fear or sense of dying, "going crazy", or experiencing a heart attack or "flashing vision", feeling faint or nauseous, or losing control of themselves. These feelings may provoke a strong urge to escape or flee the place where the attack began (a consequence of the sympathetic "fight or flight" response) and Heavy breathing.



Symptoms: Heart palpitations, Diaphoresis or perspiration, Trembling or tremors, Dyspnea, Hyperventilation, Chills, Hot flashes, Nausea, Abdominal pain or abdominal cramping, Chest pain, Headache, Dizziness, Lightheadedness, Faintness, Tightness in throat, Tunnel vision, Trouble swallowing, A sense of impending death, Feeling like one is experiencing a myocardial infarction (heart attack)



Many people who suffer panic attacks state they are the most frightening experiences of their lives. Sufferers of panic attacks report a fear or sense of dying, "going crazy", or experiencing a heart attack or "flashing vision", feeling faint or nauseous, or losing control of themselves. These feelings may provoke a strong urge to escape or flee the place where the attack began (a consequence of the sympathetic "fight or flight" response) and Heavy breathing.



Symptoms: Heart palpitations, Diaphoresis or perspiration, Trembling or tremors, Dyspnea, Hyperventilation, Chills, Hot flashes, Nausea, Abdominal pain or abdominal cramping, Chest pain, Headache, Dizziness, Lightheadedness, Faintness, Tightness in throat, Tunnel vision, Trouble swallowing, A sense of impending death, Feeling like one is experiencing a myocardial infarction (heart attack)



All persons experiencing persistent and frequent panic attacks should consult their physicians. However, many experienced sufferers treat panic attacks with some the following methods and techniques:



Some treatments include:



Diaphragmatic Breathing or Abdominal Breathing — Breathing slowly through the nose using the diaphragm and abdomen. Do not breathe through the mouth. Focus on exhaling very slowly. This will correct or prevent an imbalance of oxygen to carbon dioxide in the blood stream.



Coping Statements — repeated as part of an internal monologue such as ""No one has ever died from an anxiety attack."  or "I am frightened of being frightened, therefore if I stop worrying about being frightened, then I have nothing to be scared of."



Talking with a supportive person; someone who has experienced true panic attacks personally; someone who is highly trained in treating panic attacks; loved ones who can offer support and comfort.



Note that all medical professionals advise that if you're not sure what's happening you should seek medical attention immediately.



While it may be embarrassing to find out there's nothing wrong except being anxious its better to get checked out.



Source(s):



http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panic_attac...



http://ezinearticles.com/?Anxiety-Attack...



</answer>

<answer>



Acupuncture in experienced hands is safe and effective.  Recently a UK surgeon performed an operation using acupuncture as opposed to traditional anaesthesia.

The jury is out re homeopathy but thousands swear by it.

Have you never heard of the placebo effect?  In drug trials some volunteers are given the drug being tested,  others are given an identical  looking pill containing no drug.  Often the non-drug people show a positive response.  Even those actually conducting the trials don't know which is which.

Mind over matter?  If you believe it is it true?  Worth a try, harmless anyhow.



</answer>

<question from>



Rose22
Member since: 02 July 2008
Total points: 411 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



IBS - what can i do to make things better?



i've just found out that, after years of problems, i suffer from IBS , i know you can take medicine to help with "spasms" and pains at bad times, but i was going to try changing my diet to begin with and see how that goes.....thing is, where do i start??
Does anyone have any advice?
i know wheat could be a cause, but what is good to eat?



</question>



<answer from>



thiskid_...
Member since: 01 July 2008
Total points: 1096 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



IBS has no cure, but you can do things to relieve symptoms. Treatment may involve: diet changes, medicine and stress relief .

You may have to try a few things to see what works best for you. Your doctor can help you find the right treatment plan.

Some foods and drinks make IBS worse.

Foods and drinks that may cause or worsen symptoms include: fatty foods like french fries, milk products like cheese or ice cream, chocolate (unfortunately), alcohol, caffeinated drinks like coffee and some sodas, carbonated drinks like soda.

To find out which foods are a problem, keep a diary that tracks

what you eat during the day 
what symptoms you have 
when symptoms occur 
what foods always make you feel sick



Take your notes to the doctor to see if certain foods trigger your symptoms or make them worse. If so, you should avoid eating these foods or eat less of them.

Some foods make IBS better.

Fiber may reduce the constipation associated with IBS. However, some people with IBS who have more sensitive nerves may feel a bit more abdominal discomfort after adding more fiber to their diet. Fiber is found in foods such as breads, cereals, beans, fruits, and vegetables.

Add foods with fiber to your diet a little at a time to let your body get used to them. Too much fiber at once can cause gas, which can trigger symptoms in a person with IBS.

Your doctor may ask you to add more fiber to your diet by taking a fiber pill or drinking water mixed with a special high-fiber powder.

Large meals can cause cramping and diarrhea in people with IBS. If this happens to you, try eating four or five small meals a day instead of less-frequent big meals.



</answer>



<answer from>



michele_...
Member since: 07 July 2006
Total points: 1485 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



My boyfriend has this problem, aside from medication make sure to stay away from carbonated beverages, make sure you give yourself 2 hours of digestion before lying down, eat lots of fiber and maybe take a supplement such as Metamucil to help keep things regular.
Pay attention to your gut after eating, if you find something that triggers discomfort take it out of your diet.



</answer>



<answer from>



Lucy L
Member since: 17 May 2007
Total points: 1972 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Make sure your diet is well balanced and full of fresh fruits and vegetables. Also, lean protein, like poultry and fish, is very good. Whole grains are important, so if you are sensitive to wheat, try oats, brown rice, and other grains.

Despite the fact that it seems counter-intuititive, a diet high in fiber keeps the bowel full and functioning better. You can add other fiber like psyllium (Metamucil) or chia or flax seeds to your diet for added fiber, too.



Avoiding very spicy foods is probably a good idea, because they can irritate the bowl. I have IBS and if I cut out chilis and hot pepper, I am much more comfortable.



</answer>

<answer>



I had the same problem with my daughter. She was a magnet for the stuff. What I would do with her is to cover her hair in Olive oil (cheapest is ok just make sure it is OLIVE oil) Cover with a shower cap or plastic bag tightly clipped so it won't get everywhere. Leave about 8 hours or overnight.Wash hair with dawn dish detergent to get the oil out. Spray with Avon skin so soft bath spray. THe oil will kill any live bugs and the skin so soft will help loosen the eggs. You will need a metal lice comb. The plastic ones will not work. Take her in the sun and comb and pick. Also make sure that you pack up any stuffed animals that can't be washed for at least 14 days. Wash everything else and run through the dryer. The dryer will kill everything. Make sure to spray beds, couches, car seats with lice spray. I hope this helps and good luck. (oh you may have to do this again in 10 days if you don't get all the nits out.)
Bethany

xXx~mimi...
Member since: 21 June 2007
Total points: 1063 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



You could do, but it isn't really recommended. Swallowing tablets with water or another liquid helps the tablet to go down easily and reduces the risk of the tablet getting stuck, which could be quite dangerous and could cause problems such as the tablet scratching the throat on the way down (which would be very uncomfortable) and if the tablet got stuck due to the throat being dry it could cause you to choke and if nobody is there to help you, or you haven't got any water with you it could be very dangerous. Also, without a drink to swallow the tablet down with you are likely to gag because you will probably be able to taste the tablet because it will leave a white coating on your tongue which will taste awful. When taking tablets be careful to read the directions carefully because some tablets require you to drink a certain amount of water in order for the tablet to be absorbed into the body and so it can dissolve in your stomach. A tablet which i take requires 120ml of water on an empty stomach and if i don't do this it can cause the tablet to damage my oesophagus which can lead to more complications with my stomach etc. So be very careful.
Hope i helped :D



</answer>

<question>



What causes the skin to go black or purple when you bruise?



Why does the skin go black? Is it dead blood or something?



</question>



<answer from>



Starry Eyed
Member since: 19 June 2007
Total points: 3452 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>

</answer>



<asker's comment>



cheers



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



Abner Kitty☮
Member since: 20 July 2007
Total points: 3106 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



I thought it was bleeding inside of you because inside of you isnt blood blue? And when it gets to oxygen its red? Thats what I think..



</answer>



<answer from>



prowarlo...
Member since: 03 August 2008
Total points: 102 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



A bruise is also called a contusion (say: kun-too-zhun), and it forms because the soft tissues of your body have been bumped. Some people bruise easily, whereas others may have tougher skin tissue.

When these soft tissues are injured, small veins and capillaries (the tiniest blood vessels) under the skin sometimes break. Red blood cells leak out of these blood vessels. These red blood cells that collect under your skin cause that bluish, purplish, reddish, or blackish mark. That's where black-and-blue marks get their name - from their color under the skin.

Bruises go through colorful changes as the body begins to heal itself. The color changes mean that your body is metabolizing (say: muh-tab-o-lyze-ing), or breaking down, the blood cells in the skin. This is the process that your body goes through to repair itself.

Imagine a baseball hits you in the leg. Ouch! Your body will go through the following phases:

First, you'll probably have a bump that will look red or purplish and tender. The bump might swell from the blood collecting under the tissue. 
After a couple of days, the bruise will look blue or even blackish. 
After 5 to 10 days, it may look greenish or even yellow. 
After 10 to 14 days, the bruise will most likely be a light brown, then get lighter and lighter as it fades away. 
Most bruises will disappear after 2 weeks, and some go away even sooner. However, if a bruise does not go away after 2 weeks, let your parent know.

To help reduce swelling or the amount of bruising after an injury, apply a cold compress to the bruise for at least 10 minutes. And be sure to wear a helmet and protective pads to avoid bruises altogether!



Source(s):



http://kidshealth.org/kid/talk/qa/bruise...



</answer>

<answer from>



CARAMAC
Member since: 14 November 2007
Total points: 5724 (Level 5)

<answer>



Normally a high fever can be brought down by a cool bath/shower, then wrap up the patient and put back to bed, with plenty of blankets/liquids and keep them warm in bed.



But in your husbands case, and if he's on medication, I would give him plenty of liquids, keep the room warm and of a constant temperature, and let him sleep. Eventually his temperature will break and he should be feeling better in a couple of days, contact your G.P if this is not the case, or take him to the Emergency Outpatients Dept if he gets any worse.

<answer>



Hi Wensday!
I am prone to panic attacks myself AND I also work in a hospital in the same department where they do brain scans, lol, and I think I can safely say you will not need a brain scan (CAT or MRI scan)

First I'd like to ask you what is making you believe that you have a panic disorder? Do you have any of the following symptoms?



Symptoms of a panic attack, which often last about 10 minutes, include:

Difficulty breathing. 
Pounding heart or chest pain. 
Intense feeling of terror. 
Sensation of choking or smothering. 
Dizziness or feeling faint. 
Trembling or shaking. 
Sweating 
Nausea or stomachache. 
Tingling or numbness in the fingers and toes. 
Chills or hot flashes. 
A fear that you are losing control or are about to die.

If you think you may have a panic disorder, call your family doctor to set up an appt.  If your doctor also feels you might have a problem with anxiety, he will likely refer you to a counselor or psychologist who would do further assessment of you through talking with you about what you're experiencing and asking questions.



Depending on what they come up with, the solution may be as simple as prescribing a medication to calm you down when you feel a panic attack coming on.  That's what I have, just a pill that I put under my tongue that dissolves in minutes, and within 5 mins I feel much better, but it can make you sleepy.

So don't worry, no brain scans involved!

Good luck to you



Source(s):



WebMD.com
http://www.webmd.com/anxiety-panic/guide...



</answer>

Sell

</question from>



<question>



Front Office worker at Sports Medicine Office?



Anyone who works or have strong knowledge of the operation at Sports medicine clinic, please share some important information a front office worker needs to know --- something like terminology and other helpful information.



I am starting to work at a sports medicine office, and I need a headstart.



NO CRAZY and SARCASTIC REMARKS, PLEASE!!!!



Thank you.



</question>



<answer from>



PuterPrs...
Member since: 17 April 2006
Total points: 11933 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



What you need to know will depend on what you'll be doing. You will pick up on the terminology pretty fast, but it wouldn't hurt to take a look at some of the medical sites and get familiar with the major muscles, ligaments, and bones involved in the knees and ankles to start with - that's where you'll find a lot of injuries coming in.



You'll get a load of things like "torn ACL" (anterior cruciate ligament - it's behind the knee joint) that you'll pick up quickly. Go look up the difference between a "hairline" and types of major fracture (not "break", it's a "fracture").

You'll find out that a torn muscle = sprain, an overly-stretched one = strain. You'll also find out that one of the most common shoulder problems deals with the "rotator cuff" - look it up, it's in the joint itself. It can be strained, partially or completely torn loose, or have a "tag".

But start with knees & ankles - injuries there are the most common, especially to amateur jocks.



Source(s):



Worked for 2 years as transciptionist & insurance person for an orthopedic surgeon



</answer>

steffi
Member since: 23 August 2007
Total points: 16970 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



United Kingdom



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



When you are thirsty, do you find you are drinking pints and pints of liquid, and however much you drink, your thirst is never quenched? Believe me, diabetic thirst is demanding, and it rules your life.
If your are diabetic, there will be other symptoms. You will probably be very tired all the time, which will not ease, however much sleep you get. At your age, if you are diabetic, it would probably be type 1, and you would be losing a lot of weight. Type 2 usually affects older people, and comes with weight problems. You may also get infections which won't heal, say on your chest, or around your teeth.
There are other conditions which can make you thirsty. Can you discuss this with your Mum or Dad? You may need to see your Doctor. When I was diagnosed with diabetes ten years ago, it was like a body blow. But it hasn't been so bad. Medications are very good these days. All the Doctors and nurses I have seen have been very kind. I have to inject 4 times a day, but the needle is very small, and you get used to it. Good luck.



Source(s):



Type 2 diabetic



</answer>

<answer from>



zak's 5th
Member since: 21 July 2007
Total points: 808 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Being thirsty is the result of a number of things: The body is made up of a large % of water, so when the body needs to be replenished it lets you know by making you thirsty. If you are into cross country, you need to keep your fluids up. A good coach or trainer can help you on this one. What you eat (salty or sweet) plus certain herbs and spices can make you really thirsty. That being said, if diabetes runs in your family, it's not too early to be tested. It's just a simple blood test that is relatively painless. Your doctor can order this test for you. In the meantime, cut back on the sweets and other carbs...(cut back, not totally out) keep getting that exercise, and put your mind to rest by getting the test done. If your body isn't handling the sugar as best as it should, your doctor can advise you what to do. It's not a death sentence if you have diabetes...you just have to learn how to take care of yourself inthe most healthy way.



</answer>

Amazingw...

<answer>



When you're in a bit of a whole it can seem really tough to find your way out of it.

There's no quick fix to instantly help your mood but you say you don't have many friends and you sometimes get good highs when you stick to diet or exercise?  How about joining a local gym and signing up for exercise classes?  That way there'll be a group of you in the same class with the same goals and aims, if you start chatting to them, they'll chat back and before long you'll have a small group of people you'll be looking forward to seeing each week - you'll be happier in yourself and looking better too!

This in turn will have a knock-on effect with your outlook on work, homelife and so on.  I know I sound like a right hippy-dippy saying this, but sometimes improving just one thing in our lives makes everything else kind of click into place so everything no longer seems as grey.

<question>



Why do people get beer belly?which part of the stomach grew up actually,causing such a big big pot-like belly?



</question>



<answer from>



bitsy
Member since: 10 June 2007
Total points: 637 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Voters</evaluation>



There is a flap of skin that is right in  front of your stomach that attracts high caloried food and settles there. It is called the omentum. The more high calorie foods you eat, the bigger it gets. Thus the big belly.

Amazingw...

<answer>



A whole year of suffering? Oh my, you must be so suffering, not just from the constant bathroom visits but you probably aren't getting proper nutrion from your food so your bound to be feeling dire.

I'd throw a guess at IBS (Irritable Bowel Syndrome).  There are 'trigger foods' which can set this off, I suffered several years ago and for me, my triggers were tomatoes, beef, lamb and white bread.  It could be worth going right back to basics with your food and writing everything you eat, then writing how you feel 10mins, one hour afterwards.  You need to stick to eating a plate of one item as it's easier to see if "Carrots" make you dash to the bathroom rather than "Vegetable and meat stew".

A girl where I work suffers awfully with Chrons Disease, I've provided a link for you to check out their site as it may offer more advice.

If the pain gets really bad take yourself to Accident and Emergency, just don't go on a Friday / Saturday night!



Source(s):



www.crohns.org.uk/



</answer>

Contributing In:

<answer>



Please go to the doctor. You could have recurrent UTI's and that could lead to permanent damage in your urethra. Our bodies are great at dealing with infection, and it is possible for your body to heal a UTI on its own without antibiotics. It is also possible to have a UTI with little or no symptoms. Maybe you have had one for years and it flares up every now and again. I think you should consult your physician. Do you have nay behaviors or physical reasons that would make you more susceptible to UTI's? These are things a doctor can help you identify and you can learn to better prevent them.

<answer from>



Derek W
Member since: 02 September 2008
Total points: 119 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Hey there:
I know from experience that this sort of thing can be hard to discuss. I have no idea for sure, but maybe this is related to some kind of prostate issue? One thing for sure, is that you should go in to see a urologist to find out why this keeps happening. A few years ago I had some problems with that area as well, and some really aching constant pain. It turned out to be a urinary infection type of thing. With specific antibiotics, it was better in a few days. Again, it can be embarrassing to discuss this sort of thing with a doctor, but remember that a specialist sees things like this every day, and will be the only one who can REALLY diagnose it and be sure that it isn't something more serious. Hope this helps a little. Good luck!



</answer>

<question>



Thank you all for your advice so now what?



I will make an honest commitment to quit this 10 year drug habbit of mine. So after i withdraw and am sick for about 5 days, Depression sets in. How long does this last and what can i do to combat it?



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Depression is common after quitting a drug habit. The drugs have been so used to fitting the different receptors within your brain, and now that the brain is not being fed by the drugs, depression sets in, because those receptors are not being used anymore currently. I would go to your doctor, and ask them to assist you. There are also some support groups out there that would be able to help you with this problem as well.  Good luck!



</answer>

<question from>



ChooieBo...
Member since: 27 May 2008
Total points: 48 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



I just woke up went to the bathroom and got really shakey?



I just got up went to the bathroom and it was hurting and runnie and then couldent go pee cause it was hurting then i could once i stood up and thought i was cold or somthing and was  a little shakey then I went to bed and my body was freaking out and i was shaking the whole bed it was like a sezgur but im calming down abit atm going to go the the hospitible to see what it is anyone know? theres no pain really im not dizzie



</question>



<answer from>



csmstarg...
Member since: 26 September 2008
Total points: 563 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



STROKE?? Do NOT listen to the previous answer - it's completely wrong.



The uncontrollable shaking and cold feeling is from fever - your body is fighting an infection and you've developed an elevated temperature in the night.  Take your temperature orally with a thermometer ASAP.  If the number is 99-100, you have a low grade fever and need to keep an eye on it.  If it's 101-103 you have a moderate fever and need to see a doctor in the morning, if its higher than 103.5, you should consider a trip to the ER or a phone call to a nurse on call for your regular physician.  Taking your temperature will give you a clearer picture of what's going on, and help your doctor treat you, which is why it is so important to take it sooner rather than later.  Make sure not to drink anything before taking an oral temperature, as it will throw off the reading.



After determining the fever level, you need to take two Advil or Tylenol to reduce it, then crawl right back in bed and go back to sleep.  Drink plenty of fluids, and rest!



I can tell you what I believe is going on, but you'll need to see a doctor in the morning for sure, particularly if the fever persists or gets worse.



I believe you have a likely UTI (urinary tract infection).  This is usually accompanied by fever, and sometimes also by nausea, cold-like symptoms, headache, and fatigue.  The number one symptom - and the red flag in your cause - is pain or burning with urination.  Your doctor will run tests tomorrow to diagnose for sure, but a UTI or maybe bladder infection are the leading probable causes here.  Both need antibiotics to resolve, so see your physician ASAP!



Feel better, and make that appointment!



</answer>

<question>



Can you wake up in the middle of the night with shortness of breath from anxiety?



</question>



<answer from>



xPSYCHOx
Member since: 24 October 2008
Total points: 173 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



i think you have what is called sleep apneia....its not caused by anxiety.



</answer>



<answer from>



Charleye S
Member since: 24 February 2008
Total points: 293 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Yes, that's very possible. If you've had a stressful day or even some underlying stress that has made it's way into your subconscious, it can wake you up. Shortness of breath is generally a sign of a panic attack. You might want to start to keep track of how long your shortness of breath lasts or if it intensifies and then subsides. Check different sources for signs of panic attacks, and anxiety, etc. There are many medications that can help from short term medications like xanax to longer lasting ones, such as prozac.



Hope this helps :-)



</answer>

You seem like a very strong person that just needs some guidance, good luck and keep your head up =)

Let go of the Scissors ;)

<answer from>



Farina
Member since: 02 May 2008
Total points: 4239 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



What is the reason for your cutting? oftentimes it is deepseated urge for something a person lacks....if you can fix the root problem, you can stop the cutting....of course, easier said than done, and that usually calls for professional assistance from a person you can trust.



On the other hand, at your age, your hormones can have a tremendous effect on you. Sometimes you'll get agitated and moody for no reason. Hence, cutting sort of "releases" your stress and pressures from school or at home. Cutting can give a sense of control over your emotions, when you cut, it masks your emotions and makes you feel better, or sometimes stronger.



Keep a diary and jot down your feelings and anything at the end of the day. Whenever you have the urge, jot down reasons why you feel the way you do. If you can't seem to find a reason, it could be "that time of the month" or physical changes you have no control of--once you recognize the root cause of your urges, you can tell yourself, "oh, i know why I'm feeling this way, I don't have to do this"....



Right now, you are young, having your problems growing up, having your insecurities, entering high-school....it can be tough. But trust me, everything you make a big deal out of in your teens you will soon realize they aren't a big deal after all. This is why, at your age, you may feel cutting is bearable, but when you have to carry the scars in your young adult life in college or at work, it can cause severe regret, embarrassment...and you have to fix THAT as well. Better to stop now than later...when you reach 19 or 20, your skin will be more prone to scarring.



Good luck, and be smart in your decision. Cos honestly, cutting is stupid, no matter what reason you may have... and that is from my personal experience.



</answer>

<answer>



It isn't a bad thing. You're only 14, you still have time to grow out of it. Your leg muscles usually develop better over time. If you cannot wait and it is affecting your lifestyle, you can consider surgery, but that is typically an absolute last resort.



Braces or shoe modifications won't typically help. In a few children with a very strong inward twist of the thigh bone, an operation is possible to cut this bone and twist it outward, so the feet will point straight ahead. Surgery is only considered in very severe cases.



Good luck, and don't worry too much.
